{"code":1,"isDone":false,"toInsertArticleList":[{"createdTime":"2020-11-12 12:49:51","updatedTime":"2020-11-12 12:49:51","title":"As edtech crowds up, Campuswire bets big on real-time learning","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2072287","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/campuswire\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"campuswire\">Campuswire <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> was in a fortuitous spot when colleges and universities across the world shut down on short notice because of the threat of coronavirus. Founded by <a href=\"https://twitter.com/tadeoyerinde?lang=en\">Tade Oyerinde</a> in 2018, Campuswire is a <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2018/08/02/campuswire-launches-to-redesign-classroom-communications/\">virtual solution</a> for any teacher who wants to digitize their internal classroom communications, from Q&#38;A time to the lecture itself.</p>\n<p>The strategy, for the most part, has worked. Campuswire is now used at more than 300 universities among 200,000 students, Oyerinde tells me.</p>\n<p>While Campuswire’s pitch was set to boom overnight, the founder instead saw a bigger challenge approaching: more competition. As professors moved online, lectures <a href=\"https://zoom.us/education\">moved to Zoom</a> or tools <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/23/class-for-zoom-earliest-investors-are-betting-millions/\">built atop of Zoom</a>. Microsoft Teams and Google Hangouts filled in the gap for classrooms that couldn’t afford fancy licenses. Campuswire’s key monetization strategy, which was selling pro licenses for its online class software, felt threatened by alternatives.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>So, after months of iterating, Campuswire has adapted its monetization strategy and today announced that it is launching live courses taught by professors. Instead of solely working with professors to streamline internal class communications, Campuswire will now help teachers produce classes that students can then take for a fee. The tuition revenue will be split between the teacher and Campuswire.</p>\n<p>Campuswire courses kick off with an angel investing class taught by Charles Hudson, the founder and general partner of Precursor Ventures. Hudson lectures at Stanford occasionally, and working with Campuswire allows him to teach a broader set of students.</p>\n<p>Meanwhile, Campuswire software will be free to use starting in January 2021.</p>\n<p>The move marks Campuswire’s further dive into synchronous learning. Campuswire’s model is built on how existing classrooms work in universities and colleges. Classes on Campuswire are capped at 500 to promote conversation, and large lectures are supplemented with teacher assistant (TA) classes to hammer home confusing concepts.</p>\n<p>Meanwhile, it’s clear amid the pandemic that asynchronous learning has its perks (students can learn on their own schedule, while educators are able to work more flexible hours). Still, Oyerinde thinks a pre-recorded format is not effective for pedagogy purposes.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"3f7DFcCLcX\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/30/teachers-are-leaving-schools-will-they-come-to-startups-next/\">Teachers are leaving schools. Will they come to startups next?</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Teachers are leaving schools. Will they come to startups next?&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/10/30/teachers-are-leaving-schools-will-they-come-to-startups-next/embed/#?secret=3f7DFcCLcX\" data-secret=\"3f7DFcCLcX\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>“This is kind of the hill we&#8217;re going to die on,” he said. “Real, lasting learning has to be synchronous for the majority of people.”</p>\n<p>In other words, while there’s a small group of gifted-and-talented students who can watch a one-hour lecture and absorb every factoid and nuance, the majority of students need engagement, interaction and motivation to understand a topic, he argues. It’s the reason why MOOCs, or massive open online course providers, only have a 2-3% completion rate on their courses, he argues.</p>\n<p>At its core, Campuswire has evolved from a platform trying to compete with Zoom to a platform that is trying to compete with these MOOCS through engaging content taught by experienced professors. Its main differentiation from MOOCs is that it&#8217;s live and has teacher assistants.</p>\n<p>There are a number of startups that are trying to create engaging, celebrity professor-taught classes through hybrid plays. MasterClass, which <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/05/20/masterclass-just-raised-100-million-for-celebrity-fueled-content/\">just raised $100 million</a> a few months ago, sells entertainment and education in one go, offering cooking classes from Gordon Ramsay and tennis lessons from Serena Williams. While you can’t interact with Ramsay or Williams, you can chat with fellow classmates.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"yiPcKbVCcG\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/24/the-first-rule-of-bookclub-no-boring-book-clubs/\">The first rule of BookClub? No boring book clubs.</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;The first rule of BookClub? No boring book clubs.&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/24/the-first-rule-of-bookclub-no-boring-book-clubs/embed/#?secret=yiPcKbVCcG\" data-secret=\"yiPcKbVCcG\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/24/the-first-rule-of-bookclub-no-boring-book-clubs/\"> BookClub</a> connects readers to the authors they are reading, giving bookworms an opportunity to ask about cliffhangers and character development. The upstart is still in its early stages, but founder David Blake says that readers could talk directly to authors down the road. There&#8217;s also Teachable, which got <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/03/16/edtech-notches-a-win-as-teachable-is-acquired-by-hotmart/\">acquired by Hotmart</a> earlier this year. Teachable helps any expert who wants to create a business around their expertise do so with a virtual course. Arlan Hamilton, a seed-stage investor, has a course on the platform.</p>\n<p>Today’s pivot signals the founder’s mindset that, in order to grow to the billion-dollar business mark in edtech, you need to sell more than software that Google and Microsoft will always give away for free.</p>\n<p>“Online learning can be 100 times bigger than it is today,” Oyerinde said. “Once you actually support synchronicity, you actually support people getting to actually interact with UCLA/Princeton/Cornell professors, not just watching them on pre-recorded videos.”</p>\n<div class=\"embed 12:49:51","updatedTime":"2020-11-12 12:49:51","title":"TikTok test lets users fundraise for charity from their profile","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2072595","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/tiktok\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"tiktok\">TikTok <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> is testing a new feature that allows users to directly from their TikTok profiles raise funds for causes and charities they care about. Those who are in the test group will find a new option when they click &#8220;Edit Profile&#8221; directing them to choose a nonprofit from a list of vetted organizations and charities, like the American Cancer Society, American Heart Association, Red Cross, ASPCA, Black Girls Code, CDC Foundation and many others.</p>\n<p>Once selected, the user&#8217;s profile will feature the charity in red text just below their bio. When a visitor then clicks on the name of the organization, they&#8217;re taken to a screen that allows them to make a donation.</p>\n<p>The feature itself is powered by charitable fundraising platform <a href=\"https://tiltify.com/\">Tiltify</a>, which handles the payment processing for the donation transactions.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>The new option was discovered by social media consultant <a href=\"https://twitter.com/MattNavarra?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw%7Ctwcamp%5Etweetembed%7Ctwterm%5E1326214677861445639%7Ctwgr%5Eshare_3&#38;ref_url=https%3A%2F%2Ftechcrunch.com%2Fwp-admin%2Fpost-new.php\">Matt Navarra</a> (crediting a Twitter user <a href=\"https://twitter.com/Sphinx?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw%7Ctwcamp%5Etweetembed%7Ctwterm%5E1326214677861445639%7Ctwgr%5Eshare_3&#38;ref_url=https%3A%2F%2Ftechcrunch.com%2Fwp-admin%2Fpost-new.php\">@Sphinx</a>). He tweeted screenshots of the feature on Tuesday, which show how users can add a charity and how visitors would make donations.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">New! TikTok lets you show your support for a non-profit org on your profile </p>\n<p>h/t <a href=\"https://twitter.com/Sphinx?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">@Sphinx</a> <a href=\"https://t.co/97jTHn4lu3\">pic.twitter.com/97jTHn4lu3</a></p>\n<p>&#8212; Matt Navarra (@MattNavarra) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/MattNavarra/status/1326214677861445639?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">November 10, 2020</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script></div>\n<p>This new option follows <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/04/27/tiktok-launches-donation-stickers-allowing-creators-to-fundraise-for-coronavirus-relief-efforts/\">the April launch</a> of another fundraising feature that allowed TikTok creators to raise money for coronavirus relief efforts.</p>\n<p>At that time, fundraising was only available by way of interactive &#8220;Donation Stickers&#8221; that users could add to their TikTok videos and live streams.</p>\n<p>When the donation sticker is tapped, it takes you to a screen to make donations, also powered by Tiltify.</p>\n<p>In addition to health organizations and other well-known nonprofits, the list of charities to choose from for the stickers included many that were hardest hit by coronavirus shutdowns &#8212; like those for actors, musicians, educators and restaurant workers, for example.</p>\n<p>TikTok confirmed the same charities and nonprofits participating in the donation stickers program are also available through the new profile feature.</p>\n<p>A number of social media platforms have directed resources and funds toward coronavirus relief in 2020, including <a href=\"https://about.fb.com/news/2020/10/coronavirus/\">Facebook</a>, <a href=\"https://www.bbc.com/news/technology-52209690\">Twitter</a>, <a href=\"https://www.snap.com/en-US/news/post/covid-19-relief\">Snapchat</a> and TikTok.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"j3E4hNeaRI\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/04/09/tiktok-pledges-250m-in-covid-19-relief-efforts-plus-another-125m-in-ad-credits/\">TikTok pledges $250M in COVID-19 relief efforts, plus another $125M in ad credits</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;TikTok pledges $250M in COVID-19 relief efforts, plus another $125M in ad credits&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/04/09/tiktok-pledges-250m-in-covid-19-relief-efforts-plus-another-125m-in-ad-credits/embed/#?secret=j3E4hNeaRI\" data-secret=\"j3E4hNeaRI\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>In TikTok&#8217;s case<a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/04/09/tiktok-pledges-250m-in-covid-19-relief-efforts-plus-another-125m-in-ad-credits/\">, it pledged $250 million</a> to support front-line workers, educators and local communities affected by the COVID-19 pandemic (<a href=\"https://www.tiktok.com/safety/resources/covid-19?lang=en\">across a variety of relief funds</a>). And it provided an additional $125 million in advertising credits to public health organizations and businesses looking to rebuild.</p>\n<p>TikTok confirmed to TechCrunch the new feature to add nonprofits to the bio is still considered a test, and represents &#8220;another way for the TikTok community to support the causes and charities they care about.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The feature was made available directly to testers in its TestFlight program and was not based on whether they were already using donation stickers.</p>\n<p>The company did not say when the feature would roll out to the broader public.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"xzjX5ie9iz\"><p><a 12:49:51","updatedTime":"2020-11-12 12:49:51","title":"Ring doorbells recalled over fire threat","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2072695","description":"<p class=\"p1\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/amazon\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"amazon\">Amazon <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a>-owned Ring devices have long been under scrutiny of privacy advocates. Now the brand is dealing with another issue entirely, as the U.S. Consumer Product Safety Commission (CPSC) <a href=\"https://www.cpsc.gov/Recalls/2020/ring-recalls-video-doorbells-2nd-generation-due-to-fire-hazard\">has posted a recall notice</a> for its second-generation doorbell. Some 350,000 units in the U.S. and 8,700 in Canada are being recalled over fire and burn concerns. The devices were on sale through Amazon’s sites and retail locations.</p>\n<p class=\"p1\">The recall comes in the wake of 23 reports of fire and eight reports of minor burns related to the model. According to the CPSC, the issue relates specifically to the use of incorrect screws during the smart doorbell’s installation. <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/ring\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"ring\">Ring <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> says the issue should not impact users, so long as they only use the screws included with the system. Incorrect use, on the other hand, could directly damage the doorbell’s battery, leading to the aforementioned issue, which, in turn, can cause bodily harm or property damage.</p>\n<p id=\"speakable-summary\">&#8220;The safety of our customers is our top priority,&#8221; a spokesperson tells TechCrunch. &#8220;We have and continue to work cooperatively with the CPSC on this issue, and have contacted customers who purchased a Ring Video Doorbell (2nd Gen) to ensure they received the updated user manual and follow the device installation instructions. Customers do not need to return their devices.&#8221;</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p class=\"p1\">The commission’s site lists the specific details for units impacted by the news and adds that Amazon is voluntarily conducting the recall. Per the CPSC, &#8220;Consumers should immediately stop installing the recalled video doorbells and contact Ring for revised installation instructions.”</p>\n<p>After purchasing Ring in 2018, the brand has been a source of controversy for both privacy and security concerns. In September, the company promised to add end-to-end encryption for videos captured with the devices.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" 12:49:51","updatedTime":"2020-11-12 12:49:51","title":"Former Dropbox CFO Ajay Vashee is joining the powerhouse venture firm IVP in January","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2072098","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/person/ajay-vashee\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"person\" data-entity=\"ajay-vashee\">Ajay Vashee <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> &#8212; who spent the last eight years at <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/dropbox\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"dropbox\">Dropbox, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> rising from the head of finance to CFO over his tenure and helping to take the company public in 2018 &#8212; is joining the Silicon Valley venture firm <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/institutional-venture-partners\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"institutional-venture-partners\">IVP <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> in January.</p>\n<p>It&#8217;s the realization of plans established long ago by Vashee, who fell in love with venture early on and has always known he wanted to return to it, though he wasn&#8217;t sure when or where that night happen. Indeed, he says that when he announced he was <a href=\"https://www.marketwatch.com/story/dropbox-boasted-solid-results-but-its-cfos-departure-is-worrisome-2020-08-07\">leaving Dropbox</a> in early August to join the world of venture capital, he didn&#8217;t know where he would land. He instead &#8220;wanted my intentions out there.&#8221;</p>\n<p>It was an effective tactic, from the sounds of things. Vashee hints that he talked with numerous firms, deciding that later-stage IVP was the best fit for a variety of reasons, including experience he&#8217;d gained at Dropbox helping to navigate the company through multiple stages of growth, including both as a private and then a public company.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>Vashee also had experience working with IVP, which led Dropbox&#8217;s Series B round, and he says he saw firsthand the value the firm brings to a deal. &#8220;They helped us build our board, they were a sounding board for so many strategic decisions and always hustled for us.&#8221;</p>\n<p>As an added bonus, he isn&#8217;t starting until January, giving him a little extra time to spend with his extended family in the Bay Area and, most importantly, with his young daughters, ages 4 and 1.</p>\n<p>Vashee, who attended Columbia and headed to Morgan Stanley as an analyst right out of college, first fell in love with venture during his second job, which was as a senior associate with NEA, where he spent four years. &#8220;I absolutely loved investing and wasn&#8217;t planning to leave to join a company, but the opportunity to join Dropbox came up, and, knowing that I ultimately wanted to build a career as an investor, it if felt like something I couldn&#8217;t pass up.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Though a generalist at NEA, Vashee says he will be focused on enterprise software &#8212; including companies focused on collaboration and finance automation &#8212; at IVP.</p>\n<p>Vashee has already made some personal bets in the area, including investing in startups <a href=\"https://getmetronome.com/\">Metronome</a>, <a href=\"https://www.mosaic.tech/\">Mosaic</a> and <a href=\"https://golayer.io/\">Layer</a>.</p>\n<p>He suggests that he&#8217;ll also be spending a lot more time thinking about the going-public process, now that many choices are on the table in addition to traditional IPOs. Interestingly, he says that if he were taking Dropbox public today, an option like a direct listing is something he&#8217;d want to evaluate.</p>\n<p>Unsurprisingly, he says a handful of IVP partners serve on the boards of companies that are right now evaluating tie-ups with special purpose acquisition companies, or SPACs, too.</p>\n<p>In either case, he stresses that companies eyeing the public market need to be prepared, noting that the &#8220;operational readiness and rigor&#8221; that was instilled at Dropbox has proved &#8220;invaluable&#8221; to the company. Adds Vashee, &#8220;I don&#8217;t think the IPO process is broken, but has room for improvement.&#8221;</p>\n<p>IVP announced its last fund &#8212; its biggest to date &#8212; in September 2017, closing at the time on $1.5 billion in capital. Given that three years have elapsed and that fund sizes have only continued to balloon, and that new partners are usually brought in just before a new fund closes, the firm appears poised to announce an even bigger vehicle any day now.</p>\n<p>One of the firm&#8217;s highest-profile investors, Todd Chaffee, has <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/05/07/longtime-vc-todd-chaffee-of-ivp-says-late-stage-scene-is-now-ma-world/\">already said</a> that he won&#8217;t be actively investing in that new fund, following a 20-year run.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"CBGAVRj8yA\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/05/07/longtime-vc-todd-chaffee-of-ivp-says-late-stage-scene-is-now-ma-world/\">Longtime VC Todd Chaffee of IVP says late-stage scene is now &#8216;M&#038;A </strong></p>\n<p><strong>What does President-elect Biden’s victory mean for U.S. immigration and immigration reform? </strong></p>\n<p><strong>I’m in tech in SF and have a lot of friends who are immigrant founders, along with many international teammates at my tech company. What can we look forward to?</strong></p>\n<p><strong>—Anticipation in Albany</strong></p>\n<p>Dear Anticipation,</p>\n<p>Glimpsing into my crystal ball, I see opportunity ahead. President-elect Biden and Vice President-elect Harris have long stood committed to important immigration changes that will directly affect the Silicon Valley tech ecosystem.</p>\n<blockquote><p><em>Dream with ambition, lead with conviction, and see yourself in a way that others might not see you, simply because they&#8217;ve never seen it before.</em></p>\n<p>&#8212; Kamala Harris</p></blockquote>\n<p>We’re appreciative of what’s to come. As my firm’s mission is to transcend borders, expand opportunity and connect the world by practicing compassionate, visionary and expert immigration law in service of the betterment of humanity, we’re looking forward to a deluge of immigration changes that will support our clients as well as innovation and entrepreneurship in Silicon Valley and beyond. Please <a href=\"https://us02web.zoom.us/webinar/register/1516050298124/WN_PAPab_RYQ2SjteikBn-aow\">join me tomorrow</a> for a free webinar as we take a look at what’s ahead for U.S. immigration in 2020, what these important developments mean for Silicon Valley, for startup founder immigration, and for recruiting, hiring and retaining top talent.</p>\n<p>I’m confident we’ll see meaningful changes in immigration for startups, founders, investors, researchers, highly skilled professionals, students, Dreamers and families under the Biden administration. Check out my Immigration Law for Tech Startups <a href=\"https://www.alcorn.law/podcast/043-what-a-biden-victory-means-for-immigration/\">podcast</a> for my take on some of the highlights. Of top priority, Biden and Harris plan to unravel recent executive orders and regulations, modernize our immigration system, and perhaps most importantly, welcome immigrants.</p>\n<p>President-elect Biden’s six-point plan for building a fair and humane immigration system includes promises to:</p>\n<ul>\n<li>Rescind Trump immigration policies, regulations and executive orders.</li>\n<li>Modernize the immigration system.<div class=\"extra-crunch-offer-container\"></div><div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=DVuEUF_yKIw:dAlebxfeYjs:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img Thompson","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn18@2020_4/2020/11/12/04-50-03-573_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn36@2020_4/2020/11/12/04-51-58-439_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=DVuEUF_yKIw:dAlebxfeYjs:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn68@2020_3/2020/11/12/04-51-58-603_2dab9693d44b6d07.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=DVuEUF_yKIw:dAlebxfeYjs:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx19/cdn56@2020_2/2020/11/12/04-51-59-525_d0ea8de74ca96c12.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn3@2020_5/2020/11/12/04-51-59-581_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/DVuEUF_yKIw":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx27/cdn96@2020_4/2020/11/12/04-51-59-558_b17d1f82666abb6e.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605156591253},{"createdTime":"2020-11-12 12:49:51","updatedTime":"2020-11-12 12:49:51","title":"Europe puts out advice on fixing international data transfers that’s cold comfort for Facebook","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2072583","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">Following the landmark CJEU &#8216;Schrems II&#8217; ruling in <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/16/europes-top-court-strikes-down-flagship-eu-us-data-transfer-mechanism/\">July</a>, which invalidated the four-year-old EU-US Privacy Shield, European data protection regulators have today published 38-pages of <a href=\"https://edpb.europa.eu/sites/edpb/files/consultation/edpb_recommendations_202001_supplementarymeasurestransferstools_en.pdf\">guidance</a> for businesses stuck trying to navigate the uncertainty around how to (legally) transfer personal data out of the European Union.</p>\n<p>The European Data Protection Board&#8217;s (EDPB) recommendations focus on measures data controllers <em>might</em> be able to put in place to supplement the use of another transfer mechanism: so-called Standard Contractual Clauses (SCCs) to ensure they are complying with the bloc&#8217;s General Data Protection Regulation (<a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/gdpr\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"gdpr\">GDPR) <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a>.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"twitter-tweet\" data-width=\"550\" data-dnt=\"true\">\n<p lang=\"en\" dir=\"ltr\">The Recommendations on measures that supplement transfer tools to ensure compliance with the EU level of protection of personal data are now available here: <a href=\"https://t.co/agY2BHZVku\">https://t.co/agY2BHZVku</a> For a quick overview of the different steps data exporters need to take, check out the infographic: <a href=\"https://t.co/sYTMdNgBkn\">pic.twitter.com/sYTMdNgBkn</a></p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>&#8212; EDPB (@EU_EDPB) <a href=\"https://twitter.com/EU_EDPB/status/1326538247980249092?ref_src=twsrc%5Etfw\">November 11, 2020</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><script async src=\"https://platform.twitter.com/widgets.js\" charset=\"utf-8\"></script></div>\n<p>Unlike <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/privacy-shield\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"privacy-shield\">Privacy Shield, <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> SCCs were not struck down by the court but their use remains clouded with legal uncertainty. The court made it clear SCCs can only be relied upon for international transfers if the safety of EU citizens&#8217; data can be guaranteed. It also said EU regulators have a duty to intervene when they suspect data is flowing to a location where it will not be safe &#8212; meaning options for data transfers out of the EU have both reduced in number and increased in complexity.</p>\n<p>One company that&#8217;s said it&#8217;s waiting for the EDPB guidance is <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/23/facebook-denies-it-will-pull-service-in-europe-over-data-transfer-ban/\">Facebook</a>. It&#8217;s already faced a preliminary order to stop transferring EU users data to the US. It petitioned the Irish courts to <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/11/facebook-seeks-fresh-legal-delay-to-block-order-to-suspend-its-transatlantic-data-transfers/\">obtain a stay</a> as it seeks a judicial review of its data protection regulator&#8217;s process. It has also brought out its lobbying big guns &#8212; former UK deputy PM and ex-MEP Nick Clegg &#8212; to try to pressure EU lawmakers over the issue.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"qvFN2ZcPJr\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/23/facebook-denies-it-will-pull-service-in-europe-over-data-transfer-ban/\">Facebook denies it will pull service in Europe over data transfer ban</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Facebook denies it will pull service in Europe over data transfer ban&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/23/facebook-denies-it-will-pull-service-in-europe-over-data-transfer-ban/embed/#?secret=qvFN2ZcPJr\" data-secret=\"qvFN2ZcPJr\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Most likely the tech giant is hoping for a &#8216;<a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/11/eu-us-privacy-shield-is-dead-long-live-privacy-shield/\">Privacy Shield 2.0</a>&#8216; to be cobbled together and slapped into place to paper over the gap between EU fundamental rights and US surveillance law.</p>\n<p>But the Commission has <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/03/no-quick-fix-for-transatlantic-data-transfers-says-ec/\">warned</a> there won&#8217;t be a quick fix this time.</p>\n<p>Changes to US surveillance law are slated as necessary &#8212; which means zero chance of <em>anything</em> happening before the Biden administration takes the reins next year. So the legal uncertainty around EU-US transfers is set to stretch well into next year at a minimum. (<a href=\"https://pro.politico.eu/news/joe-biden-win-kicks-us-eu-privacy-deal-into-long-grass\">Politico</a> suggests a new data deal isn&#8217;t likely in the first half of 2021.)</p>\n<p>In the meanwhile, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/08/18/eu-websites-use-of-google-analytics-and-facebook-connect-targeted-by-post-schrems-ii-privacy-complaints/\">legal challenges</a> to ongoing EU-US transfers are stacking up &#8212; at the same time as EU regulators know they have a legal duty to intervene when data is at risk.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Standard contractual clauses and other transfer tools mentioned under Article 46 GDPR do not operate in a vacuum,&#8221; the EDPB warns in an executive summary. &#8220;The Court states that controllers or processors, acting as exporters, are responsible for verifying, on a case-by-case basis and, where appropriate, in collaboration with the importer in the third country, if the law or practice of the third country impinges on the effectiveness of the appropriate safeguards contained in the Article 46 GDPR transfer tools.</p>\n<p>&#8220;In those cases, the Court still leaves open the possibility for exporters to implement supplementary measures that fill these gaps in the protection and bring it up to the level required by EU law. The Court does not specify which measures these could be. However, the Court underlines that exporters will need to identify them on a case-by-case basis. This is in line with the principle of accountability of Article 5.2 GDPR, which requires controllers to be responsible for, and be able to demonstrate compliance with the GDPR principles relating to processing of personal data.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The EDPB&#8217;s recommendations set out a series of steps for data exporters to take as they go through the complex task of determining whether their particular transfer can play nice with EU data protection law.</p>\n<h2>Six steps but no one-size-fits-all fix</h2>\n<p>The basic overview of the process it&#8217;s advising is: <strong>Step 1)</strong> map all intended international transfers; <strong>step 2)</strong> verify the transfer tools you want to use; <strong>step 3)</strong> assess whether there&#8217;s anything in the law/practice of the destination third country which &#8220;may impinge on the effectiveness of the appropriate safeguards of the transfer tools you are relying on, in the context of your specific transfer&#8221;, as it puts it; <strong>step 4)</strong> identify and adopt supplementary measure/s to bring the level of protection up to &#8216;essential equivalent&#8217; with EU law; <strong>step 5)</strong> take any formal procedural steps required to adopt the supplementary measure/s; <strong>step 6)</strong> periodically re-evaluate the level of data protection and monitor any relevant developments.</p>\n<p>In short, this is going to involve both a lot of work &#8212; and ongoing work. tl;dr: Your duty to watch over the safety of European users&#8217; data is never done.</p>\n<p>Moreover, the EDPB makes it clear that there very well may not be <em>any</em> supplementary measures to cover a particular transfer in legal glory.</p>\n<p>&#8220;You may ultimately find that no supplementary measure can ensure an essentially equivalent level of protection for your specific transfer,&#8221; it warns. &#8220;In those cases where no supplementary measure is suitable, you must avoid, suspend or terminate the transfer to avoid compromising the level of protection of the personal data. You should also conduct this assessment of supplementary measures with due diligence and document it.&#8221;</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"epZuhO914n\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/17/clouds-gather-over-us-cloud-services-after-cjeu-ruling/\">Legal clouds gather over US cloud services, after CJEU ruling</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Legal clouds gather over US cloud services, after CJEU ruling&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/17/clouds-gather-over-us-cloud-services-after-cjeu-ruling/embed/#?secret=epZuhO914n\" data-secret=\"epZuhO914n\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>In instances where supplementary measures <em>could</em> suffice the EDPB says they may have &#8220;a contractual, technical or organisational nature&#8221; &#8212; or, indeed, a combination of some or all of those.</p>\n<p>&#8220;Combining diverse measures in a way that they support and build on each other may enhance the level of protection and may therefore contribute to reaching EU standards,&#8221; it suggests.</p>\n<p>However it also goes on to state fairly plainly that technical measures are likely to be the most robust tool against the threat posed by foreign surveillance. But that in turn means there are necessarily limits on the business models that can tap in &#8212; anyone wanting to decrypt and process data for themselves in the US, for instance, (hi Facebook!) isn&#8217;t going to find much comfort here.</p>\n<p>The guidance goes on to include some sample scenarios where it suggests supplementary measures <em>might</em> suffice to render an international transfer legal.</p>\n<p>Such as data storage in a third country where there&#8217;s no access to decrypted data at the destination and keys are held by the data exporter (or by a trusted entity in the EEA or in a third country that&#8217;s considered to have an adequate level of protection for data); or the transfer of pseudonymised data &#8212; so individuals can no longer be identified (which means ensuring data cannot be reidentified); or end-to-end encrypted data transiting third countries via encrypted transfer (again data must not be able to be decrypted in a jurisdiction that lacks adequate protection; the EDPB also specifies that the existence of any &#8216;backdoors&#8217; in hardware or software must have been ruled out, although it&#8217;s not clear how that could be done).</p>\n<p>Another section of the document discusses scenarios in which <em>no</em> effective supplementary measures could be found &#8212; such as transfers to cloud service providers (or similar) which require access to the data in the clear and where &#8220;the power granted to public authorities of the recipient country to access the transferred data goes beyond what is necessary and proportionate in a democratic society&#8221;.</p>\n<p>Again, this is a bit of the document that looks very bad for Facebook.</p>\n<p>&#8220;The EDPB is, considering the current state of the art, incapable of envisioning an effective technical measure to prevent that access from infringing on data subject rights,&#8221; it writes on that, adding that it &#8220;does not rule out that further technological development may offer measures that achieve the intended business purposes, without requiring access in the clear&#8221;.</p>\n<p>&#8220;In the given scenarios, where unencrypted personal data is technically necessary for the provision of the service by the processor, transport encryption and data-at-rest encryption even taken together, do not constitute a supplementary measure that ensures an essentially equivalent level of protection if the data importer is in possession of the cryptographic keys,&#8221; the EDPB further notes.</p>\n<p>It also makes it clear that supplementary contractual clauses aren&#8217;t any kind of get-out on this front &#8212; so, no, Facebook can&#8217;t stick a clause in its SCCs that defuses FISA 702 &#8212; with the EDPB writing: &#8220;Contractual measures will not be able to rule out the application of the legislation of a third country which does not meet the EDPB European Essential Guarantees standard in those cases in which the legislation obliges importers to comply with the orders to disclose data they receive from public authorities.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The EDPB does discuss examples of potential clauses data exporters could use to supplement SCCs, depending on the specifics of their data flow situation &#8212; alongside specifying &#8220;conditions for effectiveness&#8221; (or ineffectiveness in many cases, really). And, again, there&#8217;s cold comfort here for those wanting to process personal data in the US (or another third country) while it remains at risk from state surveillance.</p>\n<p>&#8220;The exporter could add annexes to the contract with information that the importer would provide, based on its best efforts, on the access to data by public authorities, including in the field of intelligence provided the legislation complies with the EDPB European Essential Guarantees, in the destination country. This might help the data exporter to meet its obligation to document its assessment of the level of protection in the third country,&#8221; the EDPB suggests in one example from a section of the guidance discussing transparency obligations.</p>\n<p>However the point of such a clause would be for the data exporter to put up-front conditions on an importer to make it easier for them to avoid getting into a risky contract in the first place &#8212; or help them with suspending/terminating a contract if a risk is determined &#8212; rather than providing any kind of legal sticking plaster for mass surveillance. Aka: &#8220;This obligation can however neither justify the importer’s disclosure of personal data nor give rise to the expectation that there will be no further access requests,&#8221; as the EDPB warns.</p>\n<p>Another example discussed in the document is the viability of adding clauses to try to get the importer to certify there&#8217;s no backdoors in their systems which could put the data at risk.</p>\n<p>However the EDPB warns this may just be useless, writing: &#8220;The existence of legislation or government policies preventing importers from disclosing this information may render this clause ineffective.&#8221; So the example could just be being included to try to kneecap dodgy legal advice that suggests contract clauses are a panacea for US surveillance overreach.</p>\n<p>The EDPB&#8217;s full guidance can be found <a href=\"https://edpb.europa.eu/sites/edpb/files/consultation/edpb_recommendations_202001_supplementarymeasurestransferstools_en.pdf\">here</a>.</p>\n<p>We&#8217;ve also reached out to Facebook to ask what next steps it&#8217;ll be taking over its EU-US data transfers in light of the EDPB guidance and will update this report with any response. <strong>Update:</strong> Facebook has now sent this statement: &#8220;The CJEU ruled that Standard Contractual Clauses are a valid legal mechanism for the transfer of data from the EU, including to the US. We note that new guidelines on supplementary measures have been submitted for consultation and, like many other companies, will be reviewing them carefully.”</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"UqgME289bo\"><p><a src=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/Un_6nnbXK38\" height=\"1\" width=\"1\" alt=\"\"/>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Wed, 11 Nov 2020 17:38:10 +0000","feedId":26,"bgimg":"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI","linkMd5":"b9bd6dad207340a8afc878e3b6fcfb56","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn18@2020_4/2020/11/12/04-50-03-573_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","destWidth":59,"destHeight":24,"sourceBytes":990,"destBytes":324,"author":"Natasha Lomas","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn18@2020_4/2020/11/12/04-50-03-573_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn36@2020_4/2020/11/12/04-51-58-439_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=Un_6nnbXK38:3E9g7sXgqFg:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn52@2020_5/2020/11/12/04-51-59-505_9553a6a685f441bf.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=Un_6nnbXK38:3E9g7sXgqFg:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn67@2020_4/2020/11/12/04-51-58-595_2d4d99a7bbe9c158.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn3@2020_5/2020/11/12/04-51-59-581_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/Un_6nnbXK38":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx32/cdn83@2020_5/2020/11/12/04-51-59-544_39d15c131c4da004.webp"},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605156591256},{"createdTime":"2020-11-12 12:49:51","updatedTime":"2020-11-12 12:49:51","title":"London and SF have become Impact Tech hubs, with 280% increase in VC in 5 years","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2072867","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\">New research has found that San Francisco and London have become two of the world’s leading hubs for VC investment into tech solutions that address one or more of the 17 <a href=\"https://sdgs.un.org/goals\">UN’s Sustainable Development Goals</a> (SDG), more commonly referred to as &#8220;Impact Tech&#8221;. They are followed by Paris, Berlin, Stockholm, Shanghai and Beijing.</p>\n<p>Tech solutions for such pressing issues as the climate crisis and social inequality have seen a 280% increase in global VC investment from 2015 to 2020, while investment in this space more than doubled in both cities over the past five years. The report was put together by <a href=\"https://www.londonandpartners.com/\">London &#38; Partners</a> and <a href=\"https://dealroom.co/\">Dealroom</a> as part of this week’s <a href=\"https://www.svc2uk.com/\">Silicon Valley Comes to the UK</a> virtual event. More than 5,000 startups were surveyed to create the data.</p>\n<p>According to the research, VC investment into London-based impact tech startups has grown by almost 800% (7.8 times) since 2015, compared to 3.1 times in Europe as a whole. 2020 is set to be a record year for London’s impact tech companies, which have received $1.2 billion in VC investment from January to October, already matching 2019 levels. London’s impact firms have also secured 429 deals between 2015 and 2020, more than any other city globally.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"WHLz88WQg7\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/04/15/gousto-a-uk-meal-kit-service-raises-another-41m-as-business-booms-under-lockdown/\">Gousto, a UK meal-kit service, raises another $41M as business booms under lockdown</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Gousto, a UK meal-kit service, raises another $41M as business booms under lockdown&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/04/15/gousto-a-uk-meal-kit-service-raises-another-41m-as-business-booms-under-lockdown/embed/#?secret=WHLz88WQg7\" data-secret=\"WHLz88WQg7\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>San Francisco’s impact-based tech companies have also shown strong growth over the past five years, with the data revealing that VC investment into its impact tech companies has almost tripled (2.8 times) from 2015 to 2020. So far this year, SF-based impact tech companies attracted $1.7 billion of VC investment in 2020 &#8212; more than any other city globally. At a national level, the United States received more VC funding for impact tech companies than any other country in the past five years, with investors pumping $35.8 billion into U.S. firms since 2015, double the amount invested into China ($16.8 billion) and the United Kingdom ($6.1 billion).</p>\n<p>The research also found that the U.K. capital has produced 241 impact startups since 2006, with 95 companies founded in San Francisco. In London, &#8220;impact unicorns&#8221; include Octopus Energy (green energy), Arrival (zero-emission, public transportation vehicles), Gousto (food) and Babylon Health (AI health tech).</p>\n<p>Climate change and clean energy solutions have attracted the most interest from investors in both cities, making up over 50% of overall VC investment over the last five years. Funding rounds including at least one North American investor made up $234 million of VC investment so far this year in London, up from $85 million in 2018, and equating to a fifth of all VC investment into London’s impact startups.</p>\n<p>Funding rounds for London impact companies involving North American investors in 2020 include a $118 million growth equity round into Arrival by BlackRock, an $80 million Series B round for COMPASS Pathways and a $25 million Series C funding for Tractable.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"FsLNhB6fO5\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/02/27/tractable-claims-25m-to-sell-damage-assessing-ais-to-more-insurance-giants/\">Tractable claims $25M to sell damage-assessing AIs to more insurance giants</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Tractable claims $25M to sell damage-assessing AIs to more insurance giants&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/02/27/tractable-claims-25m-to-sell-damage-assessing-ais-to-more-insurance-giants/embed/#?secret=FsLNhB6fO5\" data-secret=\"FsLNhB6fO5\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Meanwhile, impact startups are crossing the pond in both directions. Arrival is now operating in Los Angeles, while Octopus Energy launched in the U.S. market in September after closing a $360 million funding round in April and acquiring Silicon Valley-based startup Evolve Energy. And San Francisco-based Allbirds, the sustainable shoe retailer, opened its first European flagship store in London in July 2018.</p>\n<p>Commenting, Janet Coyle, managing director for business, London &#38; Partners said: “San Francisco and London are two of the world’s top hubs for innovation and technology. But today’s figures also show that they are leading the way in creating purpose-driven companies striving to tackle some of the most pressing environmental and social challenges.”</p>\n<p>&#160;</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=Gpmf53GFf_Q:AosMIviYJ9E:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img id=\"speakable-summary\">Rivian is opening up pre-orders for three editions of its upcoming electric pickup truck and SUV that start as low as $67,500 and with a battery range of more than 300 miles. However, more options will follow, including a base version that will have a smaller range of at least 250 miles and a price below $67,000.</p>\n<p>Information on the three editions and their accompanying equipment packages, paint options and pricing is just a few of the <a href=\"https://stories.rivian.com/time-to-build\">numerous details</a> released Wednesday on Rivian&#8217;s website. Perhaps one of the more notable tidbits include the addition of cheaper base version of the pickup and SUV, the official inclusion of the camp kitchen accessory and confirmation that a battery pack capable of more than 400 miles will be offered at some point in the future.</p>\n<p>Rivian, which has attracted investment from the likes of Ford, Amazon, funds managed by BlackRock, T. Rowe Price and Associates and Cox Automotive, is aiming to become the first to bring an EV pickup truck to market. But it&#8217;s facing competition from legacy automakers such as GM as well as Tesla, which says it will start production of its futuristic looking Cybertruck in late 2021. Ford is also planning to bring an all-electric F-150 pickup truck to market in 2022.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2072899\" style=\"width: 610px\" class=\"wp-caption alignnone\"><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/rivian-c.gif\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2072899\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"wp-image-2072899 size-full\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/rivian-c.gif\" alt=\"rivian interior gif\" width=\"600\" height=\"375\" /></a><p id=\"caption-attachment-2072899\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits:</strong> Rivian</p></div></p>\n<p>Deliveries of the first and, so far, most expensive version of the pickup truck called the Launch edition will begin in June 2021. The Launch edition of the RT1 truck will start at $75,000 (that&#8217;s before federal tax incentives are applied) and be able to travel more than 300 miles on the standard battery. The Launch edition will also have a special paint color called &#8220;Launch Green&#8221; along with other special badging and 20-inch all-terrain or 22-inch sport wheel upgrades included.</p>\n<p>Tho other packages — the Adventure and Explore — will be offered for the RT1 truck and the R1S SUV. All of these versions will have more than 300 miles of range. The big differences come in the finishes. The Launch and Adventure editions, for instance, come standard with an off-road upgrade with reinforced underbody shield, dual front bumper tow hooks and air compressor as well as &#8220;compass yellow&#8221; interior accents, 100% recycled microfiber headliner and &#8220;Chilewich floor mats.&#8221;</p>\n<p>The various pickup truck editions range between $75,000 and $67,500 in price. The R1S SUV prices range between $77,500 and $70,000. And all of these editions will arrive in the marketplace at different times between June 2021 and into January 2022.</p>\n<p>Customers who place pre-orders now, which requires a $1,000 deposit, will have access to a configurator November 16. Everyone else will have access to the configurator, which allows customers to pick the paint color, equipment package and other details, on November 23.</p>\n<p>The bigger 400-plus mile battery will come to the pickup truck first, starting in January 2022, according to Rivian. A longer range R1S SUV with both five- and seven-passenger seating will be announced following start of production, the id=\"speakable-summary\">Snapchat is the quintessential consumer app: With an array of fun filters, it encourages people to send fun, disappearing messages to friends and has a large base of younger users. But could parent company <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/snapchat\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"snapchat\">Snap <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> be eyeing up ways of leveraging its traction in the consumer world &#8212; with the app now seeing <a href=\"https://investor.snap.com/news/news-details/2020/Snap-Inc.-Announces-Third-Quarter-2020-Financial-Results/default.aspx#:~:text=Financial%20Highlights&#38;text=Revenue%20increased%2052%25%20to%20%24679,million%20in%20the%20prior%20year.\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">249 million</a> daily active users &#8212; with an entry into more services for business?</p>\n<p>TechCrunch has learned and confirmed that Snap is acquiring a startup called <a href=\"http://voca.ai\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Voca.ai</a>, which builds AI-based voice assistants for customer support services, <del>for $120 million: $70 million in cash plus $50 million in stock</del>. Update: Another close source insists the price is just $70 million, calculating all the elements of the deal. We&#8217;re still digging on this&#8230;</p>\n<p>&#8220;7 out of 10 customers still prefer speaking with an agent,&#8221; Voca notes on its site. &#8220;Voca offers natural, human-like conversations that will leave you wondering if you spoke with a virtual or human agent.&#8221; The platform serves as a kind of triage system, which handles simple inbound queries, and then hands over to agents seamlessly for more complex issues.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>A spokesperson for Snap declined to comment for this article, and messages sent to Voca&#8217;s founders &#8212; Einav Itamar and Alan Bekker &#8212; have not been returned. But we have confirmed the price and deal with multiple sources close to the transaction.</p>\n<p>Israeli publication <a href=\"https://www.calcalistech.com/ctech/articles/0,7340,L-3870810,00.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Calcalist</a> first reported on the transaction.</p>\n<p><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/voca\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"voca\">Voca.ai&#8217;s <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> team of 40 will all be joining Snap, we have been told.</p>\n<p>Voca.ai, founded in Israel with offices also in New York &#8212; had raised about $6 million &#8212; including a <a href=\"https://www.prnewswire.com/news-releases/vocaai-secures-investment-from-american-express-ventures-to-build-the-contact-center-of-the-future-300943535.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">strategic round from American Express Ventures</a> in October 2019. Other investors include lool ventures and Flint Capital.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"73KeZySHyH\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/12/08/snapchat-cameo-edits-your-face-into-videos/\">Snapchat Cameos edit your face into videos</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Snapchat Cameos edit your face into videos&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/12/08/snapchat-cameo-edits-your-face-into-videos/embed/#?secret=73KeZySHyH\" data-secret=\"73KeZySHyH\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>It&#8217;s notable that the startup already has a substantial list of customers and says that it powers &#8220;millions of conversations.&#8221; Specifically in October last year, it noted that it was processing some 2 million calls/conversations per month in verticals that include banking, telecoms, insurance and legal services. Customers include Toshiba, Amdocs, FirstClass Capital and Boost Health Insurance, among others.</p>\n<p>It&#8217;s not clear what Snap intends to do with Voca.ai, but the deal comes at a very interesting moment. <span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">All virtual services have seen a big boost of activity this year, with the pandemic &#8212; and the general public health push to reduce in-person contacts &#8212; driving more people to handle business online than ever before. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">And that is driving companies building consumer-facing tech apps to diversify and market their platforms as a unique way to interface between businesses and customers. One key example of that has been Facebook, which has added more tools to Messenger, WhatsApp and Instagram to make the apps more useful to businesses that want not just to market themselves to customers, but to use the apps to handle questions from them, and potentially sell things to them. </span></p>\n<p><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">Although Snap may be interested in Voca.ai simply as a way to build better interactions with its own customers &#8212; it registered a 52% growth in revenues this past quarter (<a href=\"https://investor.snap.com/news/news-details/2020/Snap-Inc.-Announces-Third-Quarter-2020-Financial-Results/default.aspx#:~:text=Financial%20Highlights&#38;text=Revenue%20increased%2052%25%20to%20%24679,million%20in%20the%20prior%20year.\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Q3</a>), and $679 million in business is nothing to sniff at &#8212; it&#8217;s a natural and logical move for it to consider how it could build more business services into Snapchat, and diversify its own revenues along with that. </span></p>\n<p>In its home page for its business services, the company notes that &#8220;<span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">People use Snapchat to communicate with friends, build relationships, play and learn. Inspire action with full-screen, digital ads that boost awareness, drive conversions, and generate real results for businesses of all sizes.&#8221; It&#8217;s not a stretch to think that those business imperatives could also extend to &#8220;drive conversations.&#8221;</span></p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"ZrHQZOPSAx\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/01/03/snapchat-quietly-acquired-ai-factory-the-company-behind-its-new-cameos-feature-for-166m/\">Snapchat quietly acquired AI Factory, the company behind its new Cameos feature, for $166M</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Snapchat quietly acquired AI Factory, the company behind its new Cameos feature, for $166M&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/01/03/snapchat-quietly-acquired-ai-factory-the-company-behind-its-new-cameos-feature-for-166m/embed/#?secret=ZrHQZOPSAx\" data-secret=\"ZrHQZOPSAx\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<div class=\"css-gyzy36-callsToActionWrapperClassName\">\n<div><span style=\"font-size: 1.125rem; letter-spacing: -0.1px;\">It&#8217;s worth also pointing out that Voca.ai&#8217;s platform is particularly relevant in the current market. At the start of the COVID-19 pandemic, businesses got quickly overwhelmed with inbound customer requests &#8212; many coming online but through all channels &#8212; and they have subsequently been looking for cost-effective ways to handle those much higher, unexpected volumes of inbound calls and questions. Voca.ai is part of the wave of startups that are looking to provide that solution, by way of AI-based voice bots to complement existing customer service teams.</span></div>\n</div>\n<p>Snap has made a number of interesting deals to pick up IP in the area of artificial intelligence, but much of that has been in the area of computer vision, for example to create photo and video filters and other augmented reality applications. They have included the likes of <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2019/12/08/snapchat-cameo-edits-your-face-into-videos/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Looksery</a>, <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2016/12/25/snapchat-has-quietly-acquired-an-israeli-startup-for-a-reported-30-million-to-40-million/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener noreferrer\">Cimagine</a>, which happens to be another startup out of Israel.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=L_6rVUZT7Lk:XHpNT0WgqL4:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img Lunden","articleImgCdnMap":{"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=2mJPEYqXBVI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn18@2020_4/2020/11/12/04-50-03-573_cda007d67cf2c798.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=7Q72WNTAKBA":null,"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=yIl2AUoC8zA":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx18/cdn36@2020_4/2020/11/12/04-51-58-439_ae8500a395ae4c74.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=L_6rVUZT7Lk:XHpNT0WgqL4:-BTjWOF_DHI":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx2/cdn71@2020_5/2020/11/12/04-51-58-537_a7ce8665622a638f.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?i=L_6rVUZT7Lk:XHpNT0WgqL4:D7DqB2pKExk":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx/cdn48@2020_1/2020/11/12/04-51-58-570_f78536c61b176c13.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?d=qj6IDK7rITs":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx12/cdn3@2020_5/2020/11/12/04-51-59-581_749e2568e12b832a.webp","http://feeds.feedburner.com/~r/Techcrunch/~4/L_6rVUZT7Lk":null},"publishedOrCreatedDate":1605156591258},{"createdTime":"2020-11-12 12:49:51","updatedTime":"2020-11-12 12:49:51","title":"Amazon’s new ‘Care Hub’ lets Alexa owners keep tabs on aging family members","link":"https://techcrunch.com/?p=2072645","description":"<p id=\"speakable-summary\"><a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/amazon\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"amazon\">Amazon <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> today <a href=\"https://www.aboutamazon.com/news/devices/alexa-can-now-help-make-the-remote-caregiving-experience-easier\">announced</a> a set of new features aimed at making its Alexa devices more useful to aging adults. With the launch of &#8220;<a href=\"https://www.amazon.com/b?node=21390531011\">Care Hub,</a>&#8221; an added option in the Alexa mobile app, family members can keep an eye on older parents and loved ones, with their permission, in order to receive general information about their activities and to be alerted if the loved one has called out for help.</p>\n<p>The idea behind Care Hub, the company explains, is to offer reassurance to family members concerned about an elderly family member&#8217;s well-being, while also allowing those family members to maintain some independence.</p>\n<p>This is not a novel use case for Alexa devices. Already, the devices are being used <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/08/k4connect-a-startup-bringing-tech-to-senior-living-centers-closes-its-21m-series-b/\">in senior living centers and other care facilities</a>, by way of third-party providers.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"Wnjqketfay\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/08/k4connect-a-startup-bringing-tech-to-senior-living-centers-closes-its-21m-series-b/\">K4Connect, a startup bringing tech to senior living centers, closes its $21M Series B</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;K4Connect, a startup bringing tech to senior living centers, closes its $21M Series B&#8221; &#8212; TechCrunch\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/07/08/k4connect-a-startup-bringing-tech-to-senior-living-centers-closes-its-21m-series-b/embed/#?secret=Wnjqketfay\" data-secret=\"Wnjqketfay\" width=\"800\" height=\"450\" frameborder=\"0\" marginwidth=\"0\" marginheight=\"0\" scrolling=\"no\"></iframe></div>\n<p>Amazon stresses that while family members will be able to keep an eye on their loved ones&#8217; Alexa use, it will respect their privacy by not offering specific information. For example, while a family member may be able to see that their parent had played music, it won&#8217;t say which song was played. Instead, all activity is displayed by category.</p>\n<p>In addition, users will be able to configure alerts if there&#8217;s no activity or when the first interaction with the device occurs on a daily basis.</p>\n<p>And if the loved one calls for help, the family member designated as the emergency contact can drop in on them through the Care Hub or contact emergency services.</p>\n<p><div id=\"attachment_2072679\" style=\"width: 690px\" class=\"wp-caption aligncenter\"><img aria-describedby=\"caption-attachment-2072679\" loading=\"lazy\" class=\"size-large wp-image-2072679\" src=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-11-at-12.28.09-PM.jpg?w=680\" alt=\"\" width=\"680\" height=\"336\" srcset=\"https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-11-at-12.28.09-PM.jpg 2462w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-11-at-12.28.09-PM.jpg?resize=150,74 150w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-11-at-12.28.09-PM.jpg?resize=300,148 300w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-11-at-12.28.09-PM.jpg?resize=768,380 768w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-11-at-12.28.09-PM.jpg?resize=680,336 680w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-11-at-12.28.09-PM.jpg?resize=1536,760 1536w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-11-at-12.28.09-PM.jpg?resize=2048,1013 2048w, https://techcrunch.com/wp-content/uploads/2020/11/Screen-Shot-2020-11-11-at-12.28.09-PM.jpg?resize=50,25 50w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 680px) 100vw, 680px\" /><p id=\"caption-attachment-2072679\" class=\"wp-caption-text\"><strong>Image Credits: </strong>Amazon</p></div></p>\n<p>These new features are double-opt in, meaning that both the family member and their loved one need to first establish a connection between their Alexa accounts through an invitation process. This is begun through the new Care Hub feature in the Alexa app, then confirmed via text message or email.</p>\n<p>That may seem like a reasonable amount of privacy protection, but in reality, many older adults either struggle with or tend to avoid technology. Even things seemingly simple &#8212; like using a smartphone, email or texting &#8212; can sometimes be a challenge.</p>\n<p>That means there are scenarios where a family member could set up the Care Hub system by accessing the other person&#8217;s accounts without their knowledge or by inventing an email that becomes &#8220;the parent&#8217;s email&#8221; just for this purpose.</p>\n<p>Alternatively, they could just mislead mom or dad by saying they are helping them set up the new Alexa device, and &#8212; o<em>h, can I borrow your phone to confirm something for the setup?</em> (Or some other such deception.)</p>\n<p>A more appropriate option to protect user privacy would be to have Alexa periodically ask the loved one if they were still okay with the Care Hub monitoring option being enabled, and to alert the loved one via the Alexa mobile app that a monitoring option was still turned on.</p>\n<p>Of course, there may certainly be older adults who appreciate the ability to be connected to family in this way, especially if they are located at a distance from their family or are feeling isolated due to the coronavirus pandemic and social distancing requirements that&#8217;s keeping family members from being able to visit.</p>\n<p>Amazon says Care Hub is rolling out in the U.S. The company notes it will learn from customer feedback to expand the feature set over time.</p>\n<div class=\"feedflare\">\n<a href=\"http://feeds.feedburner.com/~ff/Techcrunch?a=HmFwcri6TBQ:pQkrxPeA_aM:2mJPEYqXBVI\"><img id=\"speakable-summary\">The election is settled, but the nation is far from it.</p>\n<p>Before Election Day in the U.S., <a class=\"crunchbase-link\" href=\"https://crunchbase.com/organization/facebook\" target=\"_blank\" data-type=\"organization\" data-entity=\"facebook\">Facebook <span class=\"crunchbase-tooltip-indicator\"></span></a> hit pause on <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/09/03/facebook-to-block-new-political-ads-1-week-before-nov-3-adds-more-tools-and-rules-for-fair-elections/\">all political and social issue ads</a>. At the time, the company made it clear that the precautionary measure designed to turn off one potential faucet of misinformation would be temporary, but it couldn&#8217;t say how long the policy would remain in effect.</p>\n<p>Now, Facebook says the temporary ban will continue for at least another month. The decision to extend the special policy was implemented Wednesday, four days after <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/07/joe-biden-kamala-harris-win-2020-election/\">Joe Biden&#8217;s election victory</a> — and four days after it became clear that Trump had <a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/04/trump-election-2020-premature-victory-facebook-twitter/\">no intention of conceding</a> a lost election.</p><div class=\"piano-inline-promo\"></div>\n<p>&#8220;The temporary pause for ads about politics and social issues in the US continues to be in place as part of our ongoing efforts to protect the election,&#8221; the company wrote in an <a href=\"https://www.facebook.com/gpa/blog/reminders-for-when-the-polls-close\">update</a> to its previous announcement. &#8220;Advertisers can expect this to last another month, though there may be an opportunity to resume these ads sooner.&#8221;</p>\n<p>Facebook&#8217;s ongoing political ad pause throws a wrench into things in Georgia, where two January <a href=\"https://www.vox.com/2020/11/5/21537684/senate-results-georgia-perdue-jon-ossoff-runoff\">runoff elections</a> will decide which party will control the Senate heading into President-Elect Biden&#8217;s administration. A friendly Senate is essential for many of Biden&#8217;s biggest proposals, including a $2 trillion climate package that could reshape the American economy and push the country toward an electrified future that doesn&#8217;t rely on fossil fuels.</p>\n<p>Over the last few days, a shocking number of Republicans have &#8220;<a href=\"https://www.washingtonpost.com/politics/2020/11/10/whats-downside-humoring-him-gop-officials-unintentionally-revealing-quote-about-trump-era/\">humored</a>&#8221; the president&#8217;s refusal to transfer power in spite of an unambiguous election call and Biden&#8217;s decisive win in Pennsylvania, which cut off any potential paths to victory for his opponent. The Trump campaign&#8217;s last-ditch flurry of legal challenges have presented little of substance so far, and they might ultimately be more about <a href=\"https://www.politico.com/news/2020/11/10/trump-legal-strategy-election-435853\">dividing a nation</a> and sowing doubt than prevailing in court.</p>\n<div class=\"embed breakout\">\n<blockquote class=\"wp-embedded-content\" data-secret=\"4upZ5mM1wc\"><p><a href=\"https://techcrunch.com/2020/11/04/trump-election-2020-premature-victory-facebook-twitter/\">Close US election results plunge social media into nightmare misinformation scenario</a></p></blockquote>\n<p><iframe class=\"wp-embedded-content\" sandbox=\"allow-scripts\" security=\"restricted\" title=\"&#8220;Close US election
